## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling (materials science)
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature relationship of a material. Temperature typically modifies elastic modulus and hardening behavior, leading to thermal softening effects combined with strain-dependent mechanical response.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law (temperature-dependent): sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elasticity at fixed T)
- Temperature-dependent modulus: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (linear elasticity with T-dependent Young's modulus)
- Thermal softening linear: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 - c2 * T) (linear thermal softening of modulus)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (nonlinear strain hardening, Hollomon model)
- Power-law with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (c2 - c3 * T) (Hollomon with linear thermal softening)
- Johnson-Cook type: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 - c3 * T**c4) (combined hardening and thermal softening)
- Arrhenius thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (thermally activated softening with strain hardening)
- Exponential hardening: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(-c1 * epsilon)) (Voce-type saturation hardening)
- Voce with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(-c1 * epsilon)) * (c2 + c3 * T) (saturating hardening with T dependence)
- Ramberg-Osgood inverse: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2 (elastic + plastic combined)
- Polynomial with T: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon * T + c2 * epsilon**2 (quadratic cross-term model)
- Ludwik model with T: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * exp(c3 * T) (Ludwik hardening with Arrhenius thermal factor)
- Hyperbolic tangent hardening: sigma = c0 * tanh(c1 * epsilon) * (c2 + c3 * T) (smooth saturation with thermal effect)
- Swift model: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 * (c3 + c4 * T) (Swift hardening with thermal softening)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Strain hardening saturation → Use (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) or tanh(c*epsilon) to capture diminishing hardening rate at large strains
- Thermal softening of modulus → Multiplicative factor (1 - c*T) or (c0 + c1*T) applied to the mechanical response term
- Homologous temperature scaling → T appears as (T_melt - T) or normalized ratio form (c0 - T)**c1 for melting-referenced softening
- Elastic-plastic transition → Additive decomposition: linear term c0*epsilon plus nonlinear term c1*epsilon**c2 captures initial linearity transitioning to hardening
- Thermally activated deformation → Exponential Arrhenius-type factor exp(-c0 / T) or exp(c0 * T) modulating flow stress
- Strain-temperature coupling → Product terms epsilon*T or epsilon**c0 * T**c1 capture interaction between mechanical and thermal effects
- Initial yield offset → Constant additive term (c0 + f(epsilon)) represents yield stress before hardening begins
- Power-law exponent range → Strain hardening exponents typically fall in range 0 < c < 1 for metals, suggesting epsilon**c1 with c1 ∈ (0,1)
